## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. In chemical kinetics, rate laws relate reaction rates to concentrations via power-law or rational expressions, with possible time-dependent forcing or decay terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Reversible first-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (inhibition at high concentration)
- Time-dependent decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate constant changing with time)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (multiple simultaneous pathways)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with baseline rate)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure power-law dependence on concentration (dA/dt ~ A^n) indicates a simple elementary reaction of order n
- A rate expression linear in A with a constant offset suggests a reversible reaction approaching equilibrium
- Rational functions of A (numerator/denominator polynomials in A) indicate enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanisms with saturation
- Product of A and (constant - A) indicates autocatalytic or logistic growth behavior where a co-product catalyzes the reaction
- Explicit time dependence in the rate law (beyond implicit dependence through A(t)) suggests external forcing, photolysis, or catalyst deactivation
- Square root dependence on A (A**0.5) can arise from radical chain reaction mechanisms where initiation involves dissociation
- Negative values of dA/dt with positive A indicate consumption/decay of reactant; sign of rate constant encodes direction
- Higher-order polynomial in A in the denominator suggests inhibition or competitive binding mechanisms
